▸ 21.9.5 Bariatric Surgery Indications
[!info]
NICE NG191: BMI ≥35 + T2DM OR BMI ≥30 + recent T2DM (<10y); ADA: BMI ≥30 + T2DM; RYGB/Sleeve/OAGB = main procedures; 75–85% remission; multidisciplinary assessment mandatory; lifelong follow-up.

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] State NICE and ADA criteria for bariatric surgery in T2DM
  • [ ] Compare procedures (RYGB, Sleeve, OAGB, BPD/DS)
  • [ ] Conduct preoperative assessment
  • [ ] Understand remission mechanisms and outcomes
  • [ ] Apply postoperative follow-up schedule

2. Indications for Surgery

NICE NG191 (2023) — UK Standard

CriterionThreshold
BMI + T2DMBMI ≥35 kg/m² + T2DM OR BMI ≥30 kg/m² + recent T2DM (<10 years)
Ethnicity adjustmentSouth Asian/Chinese/Other Asian: BMI thresholds −2.5 kg/m² (i.e., ≥32.5 / ≥27.5)
Failed non-surgicalStructured weight management (Tier 3) ≥12 months
Age18–65 (consider >65 individually)
CommitmentLifelong follow-up, nutritional supplementation

ADA 2024 / ASMBS — International

CriterionThreshold
BMI + T2DMBMI ≥30 kg/m² + T2DM (no duration limit)
BMI + Obesity complicationsBMI ≥35 (any); BMI 30–34.9 + comorbidity
Asian adjustmentBMI ≥27.5 + T2DM; BMI ≥25 + obesity complications

3. Surgical Procedures — Comparison

ProcedureTypeRemission (1y)Remission (5y)MechanismKey Risks
RYGB (Roux-en-Y)Mixed (restrictive + malabsorptive)80–85%50–60%Small pouch + biliopancreatic limb bypass → GLP-1 ↑, nutrient sensing, restrictionMarginal ulcer, internal hernia, dumping, micronutrient deficiency
Sleeve Gastrectomy (SG)Restrictive + hormonal70–80%40–50%Ghrelin ↓ (fundus removed), GLP-1 ↑, restrictionLeak, stricture, reflux, weight regain
OAGB (One-Anastomosis / Mini-Gastric Bypass)Mixed80–85%50–60%Single anastomosis; simpler than RYGBBile reflux, marginal ulcer, micronutrient deficiency
BPD/DS (Biliopancreatic Diversion / Duodenal Switch)Predominantly malabsorptive85–95%60–70%Extensive bypass; greatest weight lossSevere malabsorption, protein deficiency, frequent diarrhoea
Adjustable Gastric BandRestrictive only40–50%20–30%Adjustable restrictionBand erosion, slippage, port infection, low remission — not recommended for T2DM

4. Preoperative Assessment (Multidisciplinary)

DomainAssessment
MedicalHbA1c, lipids, renal, liver, thyroid, iron, B12, folate, vitamin D, coagulation
CardiacECG, echo if indicated (HF, valve disease)
RespiratorySleep study (OSA screening); CPAP if severe
GIEndoscopy (H. pylori, Barrett's, hiatus hernia)
PsychologicalEating disorder screen (BED, night eating); depression/anxiety; capacity for consent
NutritionalDiet history, protein intake, micronutrient baseline
AnaestheticAirway, Mallampati, VTE risk (Caprini score)
ConsentProcedure-specific risks, lifelong supplementation, follow-up commitment

Team: Surgeon, physician/endocrinologist, dietitian, psychologist, anaesthetist, specialist nurse.

5. Preoperative Optimisation

TargetIntervention
HbA1c<64 mmol/mol (8.0%) if possible (reduces infection risk)
Weight loss5–10% pre-op (liver shrinkage diet: 800kcal 2 weeks)
SmokingStop ≥6 weeks (wound healing, anastomotic leak)
MedicationsStop SGLT2i (euglycaemic DKA risk); adjust insulin; stop anticoagulants per protocol
NutritionalHigh protein (1.5g/kg); multivitamin; vitamin D if deficient
VTE prophylaxisLMWH preoperative + extended post-discharge (28 days)

6. Postoperative Diabetes Management — Immediate

TimeframeGlucose Management
Day 0–1IV insulin infusion (sliding scale) OR SC basal + correction; NPO → clear fluids
Day 1–2Transition to SC insulin; reduce total dose 50–70% (incretin effect, caloric restriction)
Week 1–2Stop most glucose meds (except metformin if eGFR ok); monitor capillary glucose 4–6x/day
Month 1Off all glucose meds if remission (HbA1c <48); continue monitoring
Month 3Assess remission (HbA1c <48 off meds); nutritional review

Key: Rapid remission often within days (incretin effect, caloric restriction, weight loss).

7. Long-Term Outcomes

OutcomeRYGBSleeveOAGB
T2DM Remission (1y)80–85%70–80%80–85%
Remission (5y)50–60%40–50%50–60%
Weight loss (1y)30–35% TBWL25–30% TBWL30–35% TBWL
Weight regain (5y)15–20%20–25%15–20%
Microvascular benefit↓ Retinopathy, nephropathy, neuropathySimilarSimilar
Macrovascular benefit↓ MACE, mortalitySimilarSimilar
Mortality (30-day)0.1–0.3%0.1–0.2%0.2–0.3%

8. Lifelong Follow-Up Requirements

TimelineAssessments
6 weeksWound, diet progression, glucose, nutritional (B12, iron, folate, D, Ca)
3 monthsFull bloods, HbA1c, weight, diet adherence, supplementation
6 monthsFull nutritional panel, DEXA (baseline), medication review
Annual (lifelong)Full bloods (FBC, U&E, LFT, iron, B12, folate, D, Ca, PTH, Cu, Zn, Se), HbA1c, weight, DEXA q2y, endoscopy if symptoms
Supplementation (lifelong)Multivitamin + B12 (1mg IM 3-monthly or oral 1mg daily) + Iron + Calcium/Vit D + Folate + Thiamine

9. Exam Pearls (FCPS/MRCP)

TopicKey Point
NICE BMI threshold≥35 + T2DM OR ≥30 + recent T2DM (<10y)
Ethnicity adjustmentSouth Asian: −2.5 BMI (threshold ≥32.5 / ≥27.5)
ADA thresholdBMI ≥30 + T2DM
Best remissionRYGB/OAGB 80–85%; Sleeve 70–80%
Remission durabilityRYGB 50–60% at 5y; Sleeve 40–50%
MechanismRYGB/OAGB: incretin (GLP-1) + restriction + malabsorption; Sleeve: ghrelin ↓ + GLP-1 ↑
Pre-op liver shrink800kcal 2 weeks pre-op
Smoking cessation≥6 weeks pre-op
SGLT2i pre-opSTOP (euglycaemic DKA risk)
Lifelong supplementsB12, Iron, Ca/VitD, Folate, Thiamine, Multivitamin
Follow-upAnnual lifelong nutritional monitoring mandatory

▸ 21.9.6 Post Surgery Diabetes Management
[!info]
Post-bariatric glucose management: IV insulin → SC 50–70% dose reduction within days; rapid remission (incretin effect); dumping syndrome (early/late); nutritional deficiencies (B12, iron, Ca, D, thiamine); lifelong supplementation + monitoring; contraception 12–18m; pregnancy planning.

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Manage glucose in immediate postoperative period (Days 0–30)
  • [ ] Recognise and treat dumping syndrome (early vs late)
  • [ ] Prevent and monitor nutritional deficiencies
  • [ ] Apply long-term follow-up schedule
  • [ ] Advise on contraception and pregnancy planning

2. Immediate Postoperative Glucose Management (Days 0–30)

Day 0–1 (ICU/HDU)

SituationManagement
NPO / IV fluidsIV insulin infusion (sliding scale) target 6–10 mmol/L
Regular insulin drip0.05–0.1u/kg/h; adjust q1–2h
Existing basal insulinSTOP — IV insulin replaces

Day 1–2 (Ward, Starting Oral Intake)

StepAction
1. Stop IV insulinWhen tolerating oral fluids/protein shakes
2. Start SC insulin50–70% of pre-op total daily dose (incretin effect + caloric restriction)
3. RegimenBasal (glargine/detemir/degludec) + minimal/rapid correction only
4. Stop oral glucose medsSulfonylurea, SGLT2i, DPP-4i, GLP-1 RA, TZD → all STOP
5. MetforminContinue if eGFR ≥30 (adjust for weight loss)

Day 3–7

Glucose PatternAction
Normoglycaemia (4–7)Stop ALL glucose meds (assess remission)
Mild hyperglycaemia (7–10)Low-dose basal only (e.g., 5–10u); recheck daily
Hypoglycaemia (<4)Reduce/stop insulin; carb snack; reassess dose

Key: Rapid remission common — 50–70% off all meds by discharge.

3. Dumping Syndrome — Early vs Late

FeatureEarly Dumping (15–30min post-meal)Late Dumping (1–3h post-meal)
MechanismRapid fluid shift → hypovolaemiaReactive hypoglycaemia (hyperinsulinaemia)
SymptomsNausea, vomiting, diarrhoea, cramps, flushing, tachycardia, dizziness, syncopeSweating, tremor, palpitations, hunger, confusion, neuroglycopenia
TriggerHyperosmolar foods (sugar, simple carbs), large volumesHigh glycaemic carbs → rapid absorption → insulin surge
DiagnosisClinical (Symptom score: Sigstad >7)CGM/glucose <3.5 at 1–3h post-meal
ManagementDiet: small frequent meals, low sugar, low GI, fluid separate from food (30min), protein/fat with carbs, lie down post-mealDiet: complex carbs, protein/fat each meal, avoid simple sugars; Acarbose 50mg TDS (delays absorption); Octreotide (refractory)

4. Nutritional Deficiencies — Lifelong Monitoring

NutrientDeficiency RiskMonitoringSupplementation
Vitamin B12High (ileal bypass, ↓ intrinsic factor + acid)Annual (B12, MMA, homocysteine)IM 1mg 3-monthly OR oral 1mg daily
IronHigh (duodenal bypass, ↓ acid, menstrual loss)6-monthly (ferritin, Tsat, Hb)Oral 100–200mg elemental ± IV if severe
Calcium / Vit DHigh (bypass, ↓ absorption, bone loss)Annual (Ca, PO4, ALP, PTH, 25-OH-D, DEXA q2y)Ca 1200–1500mg + Vit D 2000–4000 IU daily
Thiamine (B1)Critical (Wernicke's risk — rapid weight loss, vomiting)Annual (clinical; erythrocyte transketolase if indicated)Prophylactic 100mg daily post-op; IV 500mg TDS if suspected Wernicke's
FolateModerateAnnual1mg daily (in multivitamin)
Zinc / Copper / SeleniumModerate (malabsorptive procedures)AnnualIn bariatric multivitamin
Vitamin A / KLow (DS/BPD)If DS/BPDAs per protocol

5. Long-Term Follow-Up Schedule

TimepointAssessments
6 weeksWound, diet advancement, glucose, B12, iron, folate, D, Ca, PTH, thiamine
3 monthsFull bloods, HbA1c, weight, diet adherence, medication review, supplementation check
6 monthsFull nutritional panel, DEXA (baseline), weight trajectory
Annual (lifelong)CBC, U&E, LFT, iron studies, B12, folate, Vit D, Ca, PTH, Mg, Zn, Cu, Se, HbA1c, weight, DEXA q2y, endoscopy if symptoms

Supplementation (Lifelong, all procedures):

  • Bariatric multivitamin (2/day)
  • B12: IM 1mg 3-monthly OR oral 1mg daily
  • Iron: 100–200mg elemental daily (adjust by ferritin)
  • Calcium citrate 1200–1500mg + Vit D3 2000–4000 IU daily
  • Thiamine 100mg daily

6. Specific Post-Surgical Issues

Hypoglycaemia (Late Dumping / Reactive)

  • CGM essential for detection
  • Diet: complex carbs, protein/fat each meal, avoid simple sugars
  • Acarbose 50–100mg TDS with meals
  • Diazoxide / Octreotide (refractory, specialist)

Bone Health

  • DEXA at baseline, 2y, then q2–3y
  • High fracture risk (↓ weight-bearing, ↓ Ca/VitD, ↑ bone turnover)
  • Bisphosphonate if T-score <−2.5 or fracture

Anaemia

  • Multifactorial: Iron, B12, folate, copper, chronic inflammation
  • Treat specific deficiency; IV iron if oral fails/intolerant

Nephrolithiasis

  • ↑ Oxalate absorption (fat malabsorption) → calcium oxalate stones
  • High fluid intake (2–3L/day); citrate (potassium citrate); low oxalate diet

7. Contraception & Pregnancy

RecommendationDetail
ContraceptionEffective required 12–18 months post-op (rapid fertility return)
PreferredLARC (IUD, implant); avoid oral (malabsorption risk)
Pregnancy planningWait 12–18 months (weight stabilisation, nutrition optimisation)
Pre-conceptionNutritional optimisation (B12, iron, folate 5mg, Ca, D); HbA1c <48; stop teratogens
During pregnancySpecialist obstetric + bariatric team; increased nutritional monitoring; adjusted supplementation

8. Exam Pearls (FCPS/MRCP)

TopicKey Point
Post-op insulin reduction50–70% dose reduction (incretin effect)
Rapid remissionOften within days off all meds
Dumping syndromeEarly (osmotic, 15–30min) vs Late (reactive hypo, 1–3h)
Early dumping managementSmall meals, fluid separate, lie down post-meal, low sugar
Late dumping managementComplex carbs, protein/fat, acarbose, octreotide
B12 deficiencyIM 1mg 3-monthly lifelong (ileal bypass)
Iron deficiency6-monthly ferritin; oral/IV replacement
ThiamineProphylactic 100mg daily; Wernicke's risk with vomiting
DEXABaseline, 2y, q2–3y (high fracture risk)
ContraceptionLARC; avoid oral (malabsorption); wait 12–18m for pregnancy

▸ 21.9.7 Dpp 4 Inhibitors

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] Classify DPP-4 inhibitors and their dosing
  • [ ] Apply renal dose adjustments (linagliptin unique = no adjustment)
  • [ ] Recognise saxagliptin HF hospitalisation risk
  • [ ] Position in ADA/EASD algorithm (2nd/3rd line, no CV benefit)
  • [ ] Monitor for bullous pemphigoid, pancreatitis, arthralgia

2. Definition & Epidemiology

FeatureDetail
Drug ClassDipeptidyl peptidase-4 inhibitors
MechanismInhibit DPP-4 enzyme → ↓degradation of endogenous GLP-1 & GIP → ↑glucose-dependent insulin secretion, ↓glucagon secretion
Agents & DosesLinagliptin 5mg OD (no renal adjust); Sitagliptin 100mg OD (50mg if eGFR 30-45, 25mg if <30); Vildagliptin 50mg BD (50mg OD if eGFR<30); Alogliptin 25mg OD (12.5mg if eGFR 30-45, 6.25mg if <30); Saxagliptin 5mg OD (2.5mg if eGFR≤50)
HbA1c Reduction0.5-0.8% (5-9 mmol/mol)
Weight ChangeNeutral (0 to –0.5kg)
Hypoglycaemia RiskVery low (glucose-dependent action)

3. Clinical Features / Presentation

(N/A — drug therapy)

4. Classification / Staging / Grading

Agent Comparison

AgentStandard DoseRenal AdjustmentKey Features
Linagliptin5mg ODNO adjustment (biliary excretion)CKD safe; CARMELINA (renal neutral); CAROLINA (vs glimepiride)
Sitagliptin100mg ODeGFR 30-45: 50mg; <30: 25mgTECOS (CV neutral); widely used
Vildagliptin50mg BDeGFR<30: 50mg ODRequires LFT monitoring (hepatotoxicity rare)
Alogliptin25mg ODeGFR 30-45: 12.5mg; <30: 6.25mgEXAMINE (post-ACS); CV neutral
Saxagliptin5mg ODeGFR≤50: 2.5mgSAVOR-TIMI: ↑HF hospitalisation (HR 1.27); avoid in HF

CVOT Evidence

TrialAgentPopulationMACEHF Hospitalisation
TECOSSitagliptinT2DM + ASCVDNeutralNeutral
SAVOR-TIMISaxagliptinT2DM + ASCVD/riskNeutral↑27% (HR 1.27)
EXAMINEAlogliptinPost-ACS (15-90d)NeutralNeutral
CARMELINALinagliptinT2DM + ASCVD/CKDNeutralNeutral
CAROLINALinagliptinT2DM + CV riskNon-inferior to glimepirideNeutral

5. Diagnosis & Investigations

InvestigationRoleMonitoring
HbA1cEfficacy3-monthly till target, then 6-monthly
Renal function (eGFR)Dose adjustment (except linagliptin)Before initiation, then 6-12 monthly
LFT (vildagliptin)Hepatotoxicity monitoringPre-treatment, then per local protocol
Heart failure symptomsSaxagliptin riskScreen if on saxagliptin

6. Differential Diagnosis

ConditionDistinguishing Features
Bullous pemphigoidTense blisters on erythematous base; ↑with DPP-4i (sitagliptin, linagliptin); STOP drug, refer dermatology
PancreatitisSevere epigastric pain radiating to back, ↑lipase >3×ULN; rare but reported; STOP if suspected
ArthralgiaJoint pain; onset weeks-months after start; STOP drug, resolves in weeks
HF decompensation (saxagliptin)New/worsening dyspnoea, oedema, weight gain; avoid saxagliptin in HF

7. Management

Initiation & Positioning

StepAction
1. Select agentLinagliptin 5mg OD (no renal adjust, CKD safe); Sitagliptin if eGFR≥30; Avoid saxagliptin if HF
2. Check renal functionAdjust dose per table (except linagliptin)
3. Add-on therapyAfter metformin; no CV/renal benefit — use if SGLT2i/GLP-1 RA not tolerated/contraindicated
4. CombineWith metformin, SGLT2i, insulin, TZD; avoid with GLP-1 RA (same pathway)

Adverse Effect Management

Adverse EffectManagement
Bullous pemphigoidSTOP DPP-4i; topical/systemic steroids; dermatology referral
ArthralgiaSTOP DPP-4i; switch agent class; resolves in weeks
PancreatitisSTOP DPP-4i; supportive care; avoid rechallenge
HF symptoms (saxagliptin)STOP saxagliptin; switch to linagliptin/sitagliptin/alogliptin/vildagliptin; treat HF per guidelines

Special Situations

SituationManagement
CKDLinagliptin preferred (no adjust); others dose reduce
HFAvoid saxagliptin; linagliptin/sitagliptin/alogliptin/vildagliptin OK
With GLP-1 RADo not combine — same pathway (↑GLP-1)
With insulinSafe; ↓insulin dose if hypoglycaemia
PregnancyNot recommended (Category B but limited data); insulin preferred
flowchart TD
    A[DPP-4i Candidate] --> B{Select Agent}
    B -->|1st choice (CKD safe)| C[Linagliptin 5mg OD]
    B -->|eGFR≥30| D[Sitagliptin 100mg OD]
    B -->|HF present| E[AVOID saxagliptin]
    B -->|eGFR<30| F[Linagliptin or dose-reduced others]
    C --> G[Add to metformin]
    D --> G
    E --> G
    F --> G
    G --> H{Adverse effects?}
    H -->|Bullous pemphigoid| I[STOP, dermatology]
    H -->|Arthralgia| J[STOP, switch class]
    H -->|Pancreatitis| K[STOP, avoid rechallenge]
    H -->|None| L[Continue + HbA1c 6-monthly]

8. FCPS/MRCP High-Yield Summary

TopicKey Points
MechanismInhibit DPP-4 → ↑endogenous GLP-1/GIP → ↑insulin, ↓glucagon (glucose-dependent)
WeightNeutral (0 to –0.5kg)
HypoglycaemiaVery low (glucose-dependent)
Renal dosingLinagliptin: NO adjustment (biliary excretion); others: dose reduce per eGFR
Key agentLinagliptin 5mg OD — 1st choice for CKD, no adjust, CV neutral (CARMELINA, CAROLINA)
Saxagliptin↑HF hospitalisation (SAVOR: HR 1.27); avoid in HF
CVOTAll CV neutral (TECOS, SAVOR, EXAMINE, CARMELINA, CAROLINA)
Bullous pemphigoidClass effect; tense blisters; STOP drug, dermatology
ArthralgiaClass effect; STOP drug
PancreatitisRare; STOP if suspected
Position in algorithm2nd/3rd line if SGLT2i/GLP-1 RA not tolerated/contraindicated; no CV/renal benefit

9. Viva Questions

QuestionExpected Answer
What is the mechanism of DPP-4 inhibitors?Inhibit DPP-4 enzyme → ↓degradation of endogenous GLP-1 & GIP → ↑glucose-dependent insulin secretion, ↓glucagon secretion
Which DPP-4 inhibitor requires NO renal dose adjustment?Linagliptin — biliary excretion; all others require eGFR-based dose reduction
What is the HF risk with saxagliptin?SAVOR-TIMI 53: ↑27% HF hospitalisation (HR 1.27; 3.5% vs 2.8%); avoid in HF
Do DPP-4 inhibitors have CV benefit?No — all CVOTs neutral: TECOS (sitagliptin), SAVOR (saxagliptin), EXAMINE (alogliptin), CARMELINA (linagliptin), CAROLINA (linagliptin vs glimepiride)
What is bullous pemphigoid and which DPP-4i cause it?Tense blisters on erythematous base; class effect (sitagliptin, linagliptin mainly); STOP drug, dermatology referral
Can you combine DPP-4i with GLP-1 RA?No — same pathway (both ↑GLP-1 action); not recommended
How does linagliptin differ from sitagliptin?Linagliptin: no renal adjust (biliary excretion); sitagliptin: renal adjust needed (50/25mg)

10. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
DPP-4i cause weight gain?NO — weight neutral
DPP-4i + GLP-1 RA?Do not combine — same pathway
All DPP-4i same renal dosing?NO — linagliptin unique: no adjustment
Saxagliptin = other DPP-4i?NO — saxagliptin ↑HF hosp; avoid in HF

Mnemonic: DPP4-LINA-SITA-SAXA

  • DPP-4 inhibition → ↑endogenous GLP-1/GIP
  • Pancreatitis: rare, STOP if suspected
  • 4 (DPP-4) enzyme inhibited
  • Linagliptin: NO renal adjust (biliary excretion) — 1st choice CKD
  • Incretin effect: glucose-dependent → low hypo
  • Neutral CV: all trials (TECOS, SAVOR, EXAMINE, CARMELINA, CAROLINA)
  • Arthralgia: STOP drug
  • Sitagliptin: renal adjust (50/25mg)
  • Avoid saxagliptin in HF (SAVOR: ↑HF hosp)
  • XA: saxagliptin ↑HF hosp
  • Alogliptin: EXAMINE (post-ACS)

▸ 21.9.8 Metformin

1. Learning Objectives

By the end of this note you should be able to:

  • [ ] State metformin mechanism, pharmacokinetics, and dosing
  • [ ] Apply renal dosing guidelines (eGFR-based)
  • [ ] Recognise contraindications and precautions (lactic acidosis risk factors)
  • [ ] Manage B12 deficiency monitoring
  • [ ] Counsel on GI side effect mitigation

2. Definition & Epidemiology

FeatureDetail
Drug ClassBiguanide (only available agent)
Mechanism[down]Hepatic gluconeogenesis ([up]AMPK -> [down]mTOR -> [down]gluconeogenic genes); [up]peripheral insulin sensitivity ([up]GLUT4); [down]intestinal glucose absorption; [up]GLP-1 secretion
PharmacokineticsOral absorption 50-60%; no protein binding; renal excretion unchanged (t[half] 4-9h); not metabolised
DosingImmediate-release (IR): 500mg BD/TDS with meals -> max 3g/day; Extended-release (XR): 500mg OD with evening meal -> max 2g/day
HbA1c ReductionMonotherapy: 1.0-1.5% (11-16 mmol/mol); Add-on: 0.5-1.0%

3. Clinical Features / Presentation

(N/A -- drug therapy)

4. Classification / Staging / Grading

Renal Dosing (eGFR-based) -- CRITICAL FOR EXAMS

eGFR (mL/min/1.73m2)CKD StageMetformin DoseAction
>=45G1-G3aFull dose (IR up to 3g, XR up to 2g)Standard
30-44G3bHalf max dose (IR 1g/day, XR 1g/day)Use with caution; monitor 3-6 monthly
<30G4-G5CONTRAINDICATEDStop; switch to alternative
UK (MHRA) / ADA / KDIGO alignment: eGFR <30 = contraindicated; 30-45 = dose reduction; [ge]45 = full dose.
In hospital: Hold if eGFR <45, contrast procedures, surgery, hypoxia, sepsis.

Contraindications

AbsoluteRelative / Precaution
eGFR <30 mL/mineGFR 30-45 (dose reduce)
Acute metabolic acidosis (DKA, lactic acidosis)Age >80 (caution, assess renal function)
Severe hepatic impairmentConstrast media (hold 48h post-IV contrast if eGFR<60)
HypersensitivityAlcohol excess, malnutrition, hypoxia (sepsis, MI, HF)
Pregnancy (Category B but insulin preferred for GDM/pre-existing)Surgery (hold periop)

5. Diagnosis & Investigations

InvestigationRoleMonitoring
eGFR (CKD-EPI)Renal dosingBefore initiation, then 3-6 monthly if <60; annually if >60
Vitamin B12Deficiency screeningBaseline, then annually (metformin [down]B12 absorption 10-30%)
LactateLactic acidosis suspicionONLY if clinically suspected (rare) -- not routine
HbA1cEfficacy3-monthly till target, then 6-monthly

5. Diagnosis & Investigations

InvestigationRoleMonitoring
eGFR (CKD-EPI)Renal dosingBefore initiation, then 3-6 monthly if <60; annually if >60
Vitamin B12Deficiency screeningBaseline, then annually (metformin [down]B12 absorption 10-30%)
LactateLactic acidosis suspicionONLY if clinically suspected (rare) -- not routine
HbA1cEfficacy3-monthly till target, then 6-monthly

6. Differential Diagnosis

ConditionDistinguishing Features
Metformin-associated lactic acidosis (MALA)Metabolic acidosis (pH<7.3, lactate >5 mmol/L) + metformin accumulation (renal failure, hypoxia, sepsis); mortality 30-50%; STOP metformin, supportive care, CRRT
GI intoleranceDiarrhoea, nausea, abdominal pain (20-30%); [down]with XR, titration, taking with meals
B12 deficiencyMacrocytic anaemia, peripheral neuropathy; screen annually, replace if <200 pg/mL

7. Management

Initiation & Titration

StepDoseTitration
1500mg OD (IR with breakfast) or 500mg XR with evening meal--
2500mg BD (IR) or 1000mg XRAfter 1 week if tolerated
3500mg TDS (IR 1500mg) or 1500mg XRAfter 2 weeks
4Max 2550-3000mg (IR) / 2000-2500mg (XR)As tolerated
XR preferred for GI tolerability; take with evening meal.

GI Side Effect Mitigation

StrategyDetail
XR formulation[down]GI adverse effects 30-50% vs IR
Gradual titration500mg weekly increments
With mealsIR: with food; XR: with evening meal
Switch to XRIf IR intolerant
ProbioticsSome evidence for [down]diarrhoea

Special Situations

SituationManagement
Contrast proceduresHold metformin at time of procedure; restart 48h post if eGFR [ge]45; if eGFR 30-44, assess risk/benefit
SurgeryHold on day of surgery; restart when eating/drinking and renal function stable
Hospital admissionReview indication; hold if acute illness, hypoxia, sepsis, contrast planned
PregnancySafe (Category B) but insulin preferred for GDM/pre-existing DM; can continue if already on for PCOS
CKD G3b (eGFR 30-44)Half max dose; monitor eGFR 3-6 monthly; stop if <30
CKD G4-5 (eGFR <30)STOP (contraindicated)

8. FCPS/MRCP High-Yield Summary

TopicKey Points
Mechanism[down]Hepatic gluconeogenesis (AMPK), [up]insulin sensitivity, [up]GLP-1, [down]gut glucose absorption
DosingIR: 500mg BD/TDS meals -> max 3g; XR: 500mg OD evening meal -> max 2g; titrate weekly
Renal dosingeGFR [ge]45: full; 30-44: half max; <30: STOP (contraindicated)
ContraindicationseGFR<30, acute acidosis, severe hepatic, contrast/sepsis/surgery (hold), alcohol excess
B12 deficiency10-30% on long-term; screen annually; replace if <200 pg/mL
Lactic acidosisRare (3-10/100,000 pt-yrs); mortality 30-50%; risk: renal failure, hypoxia, sepsis, contrast, alcohol, liver disease
GI intolerance20-30%; XR + titration + meals [down]risk; switch to XR if intolerant
WeightNeutral or modest loss (1-3kg)
CV benefitUKPDS: [down]MI (39%), [down]all-cause mortality (36%) in overweight T2DM; neutral in modern CVOTs

9. Viva Questions

QuestionExpected Answer
What is the mechanism of action of metformin?Activates AMPK -> [down]hepatic gluconeogenesis, [up]peripheral insulin sensitivity ([up]GLUT4), [up]GLP-1 secretion, [down]intestinal glucose absorption
What are the renal dosing guidelines for metformin?eGFR [ge]45: full dose; eGFR 30-44: half maximum dose; eGFR <30: CONTRAINDICATED -- stop metformin
When do you hold metformin in hospital?Acute illness, sepsis, hypoxia, contrast procedures (hold 48h post-IV contrast if eGFR<60), surgery (hold periop), eGFR<30
What is metformin-associated lactic acidosis (MALA)?Metabolic acidosis (pH<7.3, lactate>5) + metformin accumulation; risk factors: renal failure, hypoxia, sepsis, contrast, alcohol, liver disease; mortality 30-50%
How do you manage GI side effects of metformin?Use XR formulation; titrate slowly (500mg weekly); take with meals; switch from IR to XR; consider probiotics
What is the effect of metformin on vitamin B12?[down]B12 absorption (10-30% prevalence on long-term); screen annually; replace if <200 pg/mL (oral 1mg OD or IM 1mg monthly)
Is metformin safe in pregnancy?Category B; safe but insulin preferred for GDM/pre-existing DM; can continue if on for PCOS
What is the UKPDS metformin legacy effect?Overweight T2DM: metformin [down]MI (39%) and all-cause mortality (36%) vs conventional; persisted 10y post-trial

10. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
Metformin causes hypoglycaemia?NO -- minimal risk as monotherapy; only with insulin/SU
Metformin contraindicated in all CKD?NO -- only eGFR<30; 30-44 = half dose; [ge]45 = full dose
Metformin before contrast?Hold at time of IV contrast; restart 48h post if eGFR[ge]45; if eGFR 30-44, individualise
XR vs IR efficacy?Equivalent HbA1c reduction; XR better GI tolerability

Mnemonic: METFORMIN-RX

  • Mechanism: AMPK -> [down]HGP, [up]insulin sensitivity
  • Entered: not metabolised, renal excretion
  • Titrate: 500mg weekly to max 2-3g
  • Full dose if eGFR [ge]45
  • Over 30-44 -> half dose
  • Renal <30 -> STOP (contraindicated)
  • Monitor B12 annually
  • Intolerance GI: use XR, with meals
  • No hypoglycaemia as monotherapy
  • Lactic acidosis: rare, pH<7.3 + lactate>5 + renal failure/hypoxia
  • Contrast/surgery/sepsis: HOLD
  • Pregnancy: safe but insulin preferred
  • Renal <30 = contraindicated
  • XR preferred for GI tolerability

▸ 21.9.9 Sglt2 Inhibitors
[!info]
SGLT2 inhibitors: empagliflozin, dapagliflozin, canagliflozin, ertugliflozin — ↓renal glucose reabsorption → glucosuria; proven CV death↓, HF hosp↓, CKD progression↓; euglycaemic DKA risk; genital mycotic infections.

1. Learning Objectives

  • [ ] State SGLT2i mechanism, pharmacokinetics, and dosing
  • [ ] Apply eGFR-based initiation/continuation thresholds
  • [ ] Recognise indications: ASCVD, HF (HFrEF/HFpEF), CKD, T2DM
  • [ ] Manage key adverse effects: euglycaemic DKA, genital infections, amputation (canagliflozin), Fournier's gangrene
  • [ ] Counsel on sick-day rules (STOP during acute illness)

2. Definition & Epidemiology

FeatureDetail
Drug ClassSodium-glucose co-transporter 2 inhibitors
MechanismInhibit SGLT2 in proximal tubule (S1 segment) → ↓glucose reabsorption → ↑urinary glucose excretion (~70–90g/day) → ↓plasma glucose, ↓weight, ↓BP, ↓intraglomerular pressure
Agents & DosesEmpagliflozin 10/25mg OD; Dapagliflozin 10mg OD; Canagliflozin 100/300mg OD; Ertugliflozin 5/15mg OD
HbA1c Reduction0.5–1.0% (5–11 mmol/mol) as add-on; weight loss 2–3kg; SBP ↓3–5 mmHg
PharmacokineticsOral, ~80% bioavailability; hepatic glucuronidation (UGT1A9); renal excretion <2%; t½ 12–17h

3. Clinical Features / Presentation

(N/A — drug therapy)

4. Classification / Staging / Grading

eGFR Thresholds — CRITICAL FOR EXAMS

AgentInitiate if eGFR ≥Continue if eGFR ≥Stop if eGFR <
Empagliflozin20 (HF/CKD) / 45 (T2DM)2020
Dapagliflozin25 (HF/CKD) / 45 (T2DM)1515
Canagliflozin303030
Ertugliflozin454545
Key: HF/CKD indications allow lower eGFR initiation than T2DM-only use. DAPA-CKD/EMPA-KIDNEY: continue to dialysis.

Indications by Comorbidity

IndicationPreferred Agent(s)Key Trials
T2DM + ASCVDEmpagliflozin, Canagliflozin, DapagliflozinEMPA-REG, CANVAS, DECLARE
HFrEF (EF≤40%)Dapagliflozin, EmpagliflozinDAPA-HF, EMPEROR-Reduced
HFpEF (EF≥50%)Empagliflozin, DapagliflozinEMPEROR-Preserved, DELIVER
CKD (eGFR≥20)Dapagliflozin, Empagliflozin, CanagliflozinDAPA-CKD, EMPA-KIDNEY, CREDENCE
T2DM without high-risk comorbidityAny (consider cost/access)—

5. Diagnosis & Investigations

InvestigationRoleMonitoring
eGFR (CKD-EPI)Dosing/eligibilityBefore initiation, 2–4 weeks post, then 3–6 monthly
Ketones (blood)Euglycaemic DKA suspicionIf unwell, nausea, abdominal pain — check ketones even if glucose <13.9
Genital examMycotic infectionsClinical review if symptomatic
Foot examAmputation risk (canagliflozin)Baseline + annual; avoid if active ulcer/PAD
HbA1cEfficacy3-monthly till target, then 6-monthly

6. Differential Diagnosis

ConditionDistinguishing Features
Euglycaemic DKAGlucose <13.9 mmol/L + ketonaemia >3 + pH <7.3; on SGLT2i, illness, low carb, surgery, alcohol; STOP SGLT2i, DKA protocol
Genital mycotic infectionVulvovaginitis, balanitis; common (10–15%); treat with topical antifungals; consider recurrent = stop
Fournier's gangreneRare (<0.1%); necrotising fasciitis of perineum; STOP SGLT2i, urgent surgical debridement, IV antibiotics
Volume depletionHypotension, AKI; elderly, diuretics, low SBP; monitor renal function
Amputation (canagliflozin)↑Toe/midfoot amputation (CANVAS); avoid if active DFU/PAD

7. Management

Initiation & Sick-Day Rules

StepAction
1. Check eligibilityeGFR per table above; no active DKA, not T1DM, not pregnant
2. Counsel sick-day rulesSTOP SGLT2i if: acute illness, fasting, surgery (3 days pre-op), low carb/keto diet, alcohol excess, dehydration
3. Start doseStandard dose (no titration needed); take any time with/without food
4. MonitoreGFR 2–4 weeks, then 3–6 monthly; ketones if unwell

Adverse Effect Management

Adverse EffectManagement
Genital mycotic infectionTopical clotrimazole/fluconazole; hygiene; if recurrent → consider stop
UTIStandard antibiotics; ↑fluid intake
Volume depletion/hypotension↓diuretic dose; ensure euvolaemia; monitor renal function
Euglycaemic DKASTOP SGLT2i immediately; standard DKA protocol (fluids, insulin, K+); glucose may be normal — don't delay insulin
Fournier's gangreneSTOP SGLT2i; emergency surgical debridement; broad-spectrum IV antibiotics; ICU
flowchart TD
    A[SGLT2i Candidate] --> B{eGFR Check}
    B -->|≥45 T2DM| C[Start standard dose]
    B -->|≥20-25 HF/CKD| D[Start per HF/CKD indication]
    B -->|<threshold| E[Do NOT initiate]
    C --> F[Counsel sick-day rules: STOP if ill/fasting/surgery]
    D --> F
    F --> G[Monitor eGFR 2-4 weeks]
    G --> H{Unwell?}
    H -->|Yes| I[STOP SGLT2i, check ketones]
    I --> J{Ketones >3?}
    J -->|Yes| K[Euglycaemic DKA protocol]
    J -->|No| L[Restart when well]

8. FCPS/MRCP High-Yield Summary

TopicKey Points
MechanismInhibit SGLT2 in proximal tubule (S1) → glucosuria ~70–90g/day → ↓glucose, ↓weight, ↓BP, ↓intraglomerular pressure
eGFR thresholdsEmpa: initiate ≥45 (T2DM) / ≥20 (HF/CKD); Dapa: ≥45/≥25; Cana: ≥30; Ertu: ≥45
CV benefitEmpa: EMPA-REG (CV death↓); Cana: CANVAS (MACE↓); Dapa: DECLARE (HF hosp↓)
HF benefitAll HFrEF/HFpEF: Dapa (DAPA-HF, DELIVER), Empa (EMPEROR-Red/Pres) — 1st line for HF in DM
CKD benefitCana (CREDENCE), Dapa (DAPA-CKD), Empa (EMPA-KIDNEY) — continue to dialysis
Euglycaemic DKAGlucose <13.9 + ketones >3 + pH <7.3; STOP SGLT2i, standard DKA Rx; check ketones if unwell
Genital infections10–15% (women > men); topical antifungals; recurrent → stop
AmputationCanagliflozin: ↑toe/midfoot amputation (CANVAS); avoid if active DFU/PAD
Fournier's gangreneRare (<0.1%); necrotising perineal infection; STOP SGLT2i, surgical emergency
Sick-day rulesSTOP if: illness, fasting, surgery (3d pre), low carb, alcohol, dehydration

9. Viva Questions

QuestionExpected Answer
What is the mechanism of SGLT2 inhibitors?Inhibit SGLT2 in proximal tubule (S1) → ↓glucose reabsorption → ↑urinary glucose excretion (~70–90g/day) → ↓plasma glucose, ↓weight, ↓BP, ↓intraglomerular pressure
What are the eGFR thresholds for SGLT2i initiation?Empagliflozin: ≥45 (T2DM), ≥20 (HF/CKD); Dapagliflozin: ≥45 (T2DM), ≥25 (HF/CKD); Canagliflozin: ≥30; Ertugliflozin: ≥45
Which SGLT2i have proven HF benefit?All HFrEF/HFpEF: Dapagliflozin (DAPA-HF, DELIVER), Empagliflozin (EMPEROR-Reduced, EMPEROR-Preserved) — 1st line for HF in diabetes
Which SGLT2i have proven CKD benefit?Canagliflozin (CREDENCE), Dapagliflozin (DAPA-CKD), Empagliflozin (EMPA-KIDNEY) — continue to dialysis
What is euglycaemic DKA and how do you manage it?DKA with glucose <13.9 mmol/L; on SGLT2i + precipitant (illness, fasting, surgery, low carb); STOP SGLT2i, standard DKA protocol — check ketones even if glucose normal
What are the sick-day rules for SGLT2i?STOP if: acute illness, fasting, surgery (3 days pre-op), low carbohydrate/ketogenic diet, alcohol excess, dehydration; restart when eating/drinking normally and well
What is the amputation risk with canagliflozin?CANVAS trial: ↑toe/midfoot amputation (6.3 vs 3.4/1000 pt-yrs); avoid in active DFU/PAD; monitor feet
How does SGLT2i reduce intraglomerular pressure?↑Tubuloglomerular feedback: ↑distal NaCl delivery → afferent arteriolar vasoconstriction → ↓intraglomerular pressure → ↓hyperfiltration → renal protection

10. Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
SGLT2i in T1DM?Contraindicated — euglycaemic DKA risk high; only in clinical trials with strict monitoring
SGLT2i + insulin?Safe; ↓insulin dose often needed (20–30%) to avoid hypoglycaemia
Euglycaemic DKA vs DKA?Same ketone/pH criteria; glucose <13.9; STOP SGLT2i; don't delay insulin because glucose "not high"

Mnemonic: SGLT2-EMPA-CAN-DAPA

  • SGLT2 → proximal tubule S1 segment
  • Glucosuria ~70-90g/day
  • Lowers glucose, weight, BP, intraglomerular pressure
  • Thresholds: Empa≥45/20, Dapa≥45/25, Cana≥30
  • 2 (SGLT2) not SGLT1 (gut)
  • EMPA-REG: CV death↓
  • MP: EMPEROR-HF (Red/Pres)
  • AKI: EMPA-KIDNEY
  • CREDENCE: Cana renal
  • Amputation: Cana↑
  • Nephroprotection: all
  • DAPA-HF: HFrEF
  • ADAPA-CKD: CKD
  • Preserved: DELIVER HFpEF
  • All HF types benefit**
